    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/255366-being-entirely-cynical-did-this-win-the">Being entirely cynical, did this win the genre award because people like John Green? Because I rather value the Goodreads awards as a starting point in finding new books to read, and it would annoy me if a person&#39;s popularity were to taint the results.</a>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would say no. I really enjoyed this story as something that Esther wrote, as well as her family and friends. It is a truly fun, silly, but sad journ<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would say no. I really enjoyed this story as something that Esther wrote, as well as her family and friends. It is a truly fun, silly, but sad journey that I greatly enjoyed(even though it hurt a lot). I voted for it in the GoodReads Awards because I loved the writer in Esther, not because she knew John Green. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8714673340243880056">I have sat here forever trying to figure out what to say. This book made me cry in places and smile in others. But mostly it's just sad. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526173663ra/25529782.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have had this book and hundreds of books on my shelves forever. I still do. I have been trying to read as many as possible before my own fight against cancer begins in a week. I started getting mad and just grabbing a lot of books for mom to sell Monday before we go in the afternoon to get a mold of my pelvis. And... I came across this book on my shelf. I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText8714673340243880056" style="display:none">I have sat here forever trying to figure out what to say. This book made me cry in places and smile in others. But mostly it's just sad. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526173663ra/25529782.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have had this book and hundreds of books on my shelves forever. I still do. I have been trying to read as many as possible before my own fight against cancer begins in a week. I started getting mad and just grabbing a lot of books for mom to sell Monday before we go in the afternoon to get a mold of my pelvis. And... I came across this book on my shelf. I have had the hardback forever! I felt like God (yeah, GOD!) sent me back to that shelf for one more go around. <br><br>I found this book and realized it was about a girl that died of cancer. Well obviously I felt I had to read it right then and I did! <br><br>The only thing that turned me off is finding out the stuff about John Green. Yes, he wrote a great introduction but reading about how he used Ester to write his own book turned me right off. If someone inspires you to write a book about them then I'm all for that, but this just seemed weird. I don't know - enough about him. I'm glad I'm one of the few that picked up the book for what it was about and knew nothing about Ester. I guess I never read his acknowledgment in his book or movie. <br><br>I WISH there were tons more books like this - kids, the elderly, whoever writing their story about whatever disease they might have. There are a few books here and there that have been written that have some of my same mental disorders and they all helped me in their own way. This book did the same. There were things here and there that got through to me. <br><br>I also loved reading about interactions with Esther and her sibs, especially her brothers. Reading about her fangirling about Harry Potter and finding out about these Harry Potter bands and different groups of people I have never heard of in my life. I don't like social media that much and I don't watch the news or talk shows so I'm mostly out of the loop and I could care less. <br><br>I loved so much that Esther had all of these online friend in her group and her make a wish was to get together with them. Just little things here and there. <br><br>Either way, it helped me a little bit and if it does that for others, then I'm all for it. <br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel 🖤🐾🐺</span>

    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7920577-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404792415p2/7920577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/837587861?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/7920577-allison">Allison</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer837587861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6346570711005594365">Dear Esther,<br/>I just finished reading your published book. Yeah, that's right! Your dream of becoming an author has come true. I feel so honored to be a part of that goal. I woke up at 8:30 this morning to buy this book. I went in and bought the book as soon as the doors opened. (They hadn't even put the book out on display yet!) I felt honored to be one of the first to hold this in my hand. <br/>I am amazed at your outlook on life and death. I've never been spiritual or religious, so death is kinda fe</span>
  <span id="freeText6346570711005594365" style="display:none">Dear Esther,<br />I just finished reading your published book. Yeah, that's right! Your dream of becoming an author has come true. I feel so honored to be a part of that goal. I woke up at 8:30 this morning to buy this book. I went in and bought the book as soon as the doors opened. (They hadn't even put the book out on display yet!) I felt honored to be one of the first to hold this in my hand. <br />I am amazed at your outlook on life and death. I've never been spiritual or religious, so death is kinda feared for me. I was so astounded at your ability to say that death is just a part of life that you'll experience no matter what. You said that you have a hard time putting emotions into words, so maybe you did fear death. <br />I cried when you died in the book. I didn't cry because I was grieving per se. I cried because of how much you missed out on. I cried because you always wanted to kiss a boy and you never got to. I cried because you can't watch Doctor Who anymore. In books, I'm used to simple things like that working out. I guess you really put it right in front of my face that a lot of things don't work out in life. <br />You kept saying how lazy you were and how you wished you were actually helping people. You are, Esther. The foundation This Star Won't Go Out was inspired by you and know you're helping other sick kids. You're letting others learn the secrets behind life, due to how wise you were. I'm going to become an oncology researcher, Esther. I decided that a long time ago, but this book has made me realize only more how much I need to become an oncology researcher to help combat this awful dream.<br />To be honest, getting cancer is the scariest thing in life for me. I can't imagine a worth death or sentence. It seems so scary Esther, but you handled it so well. At least, that's what was present in your writing. <br />We'll miss you here Esther, but just know that you're still with us and you influence what a lot of people do. Just remember, don't forget to be awesome.<br />Love,<br />Allison</span>

<div id="review_855152815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855152815" />
    <a title="Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13400128-lynda"><img alt="Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558931714p2/13400128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855152815?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynda" href="/user/show/13400128-lynda">Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=author-usa">author-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=z-read-2014">z-read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855152815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13467581721360282879"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1393074378p8/943617.jpg' width='600' height='150' alt='esther' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>ESTHER GRACE EARL<br/>3 August 1994 - 25 August 2010<br/>[16 years]</b><br/><br/>Many readers have had the pleasure of reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars' title='The Fault in Our Stars by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fault in Our Stars</a> by the very talented author, John Green. John actually dedicated his book <blockquote> TO ESTHER EARL</blockquote> and in his acknowledgments stated <blockquote>
  <i>"Esther Earl, whose life was a gift to me and many."</i>
</blockquote>After reading both the dedication and acknowledgement, I was intrigued to find out just who Esther Earl was. It did not take me long to learn that Esther (meaning "Star") was a phenomenal young </span>
  <span id="freeText13467581721360282879" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1393074378p8/943617.jpg" width="600" height="150" alt="esther" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>ESTHER GRACE EARL<br>3 August 1994 - 25 August 2010<br>[16 years]</b><br><br>Many readers have had the pleasure of reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> by the very talented author, John Green. John actually dedicated his book <blockquote> TO ESTHER EARL</blockquote> and in his acknowledgments stated <blockquote>
  <i>"Esther Earl, whose life was a gift to me and many."</i>
</blockquote>After reading both the dedication and acknowledgement, I was intrigued to find out just who Esther Earl was. It did not take me long to learn that Esther (meaning "Star") was a phenomenal young lady. In November 2006, aged 12, she was diagnosed with thyroid cancer and had already developed extensive tumors in her lungs. For four years she endured surgery, chemotherapy, and medications as she balanced the demands of a terminal illness with a teenager’s desire for fun.<br><br>Tethered by tubes to oxygen tanks that helped her breathe, Esther spoke to the world from her bedroom via the internet (she began making You Tube videos in late 2008 under the name <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/cookie4monster4" rel="nofollow noopener">cookie4monster4</a>). A vibrant member of online communities, she formed lasting friendships with people around the world, charming thousands with her dimpled smile and cheery, loving presence. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1393070872p8/943599.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="esther1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Esther was a huge Harry Potter fan, as well as a dedicated "Nerdfighter". She invoked an iconic phrase from the online Nerdfighter community when she signed an entry, <blockquote>
  <i>“don’t forget to be awesome — love, Esther.’’</i>
</blockquote> She became a celebrity when John Green posted a YouTube video encouraging people to vote “with Esther’’ in a contest. The prize was a $250,000 grant, and the outpouring for Esther garnered so many votes that the award went to the Harry Potter Alliance, a nonprofit founded in the US that promotes human rights, literacy, and disaster relief efforts.<br><br><b>This Star Won't Go Out</b> is a glimpse into Esther's life, via a scrapbook-like biography told through Esther's own drawings, diary entries, handwritten notes, stories from her family, and a letter from one of her doctors. There is a beautiful and heartfelt introduction to the book by John Green:<blockquote>
  <i>"Esther's story belonged to her, and fortunately for us she was an extraordinary writer, who in these pages tells that story beautifully. I find comfort in that, but make no mistake: I am still pissed off that she died. I still miss her. I still find her loss an intolerable injustice. And I wish she'd read The Fault in Our Stars. I am astonished that the book has found such a broad audience, but the person I most want to read it never will."</i>
</blockquote> A few days after turning 16 and a couple of weeks before she died, Esther set aside her normal playful demeanor and mused about how difficult it is to separate the twined strands of identity and illness.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I sometimes wish I’d never gone through this and then I realize that if that happened, I wouldn’t be who I am, and then I get all, like, ‘Oh, that’s just confusing.’ But then sometimes I do wish it never happened, the cancer thing.’’</i>
</blockquote> After her death the <a href="http://tswgo.org/index.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> This Star Won't Go Out </a>foundation was created by her family in her honor to financially help other young people struggling with cancer. Additionally, every year on Esther's birthday, August 3rd, people across the world participate in Esther day, a celebration of Esther's life and, as Esther requested, love and family.<br><br><b>This Star Won't Go Out</b> is an encouraging and inspirational read about an empathetic and joyful young lady, so wise beyond her years, who loved so deeply and genuinely. She was focussed daily on a mission to comfort and care for others, and no matter what pain and agony she might have been going through, she refused to abandon her family and friends. <br><br>Esther Earl was an awesome person who did amazing things. She truly was a Star who shone light on all she met. It was a privilege to read this book; to celebrate her life and legacy.<br><br>RIP awesome girl x</span>
  <a data-text-id="13467581721360282879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/9128249-matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9128249-matt?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9128249-matt?shelf=meh-so-what">meh-so-what</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9128249-matt?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer885093198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5200023666742226929">2/5<br/><br/>Time for me to be a douche about the "girl with cancer book." I'm not actually, but some will think so from my opinion.<br/><br/>The thing is, this book isn't quite what I expected, and something wasn't sitting right with me about the book as a symbol. Halfway through I formed my opinion as to why. I'll explain.<br/><br/>This states most of my case:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851057221?book_show_action=false&page=1'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br/><br/>The gripes of the above reviewer mirror most of my concerns but there's more to it than that. I have another beef with the pub</span>
  <span id="freeText5200023666742226929" style="display:none">2/5<br /><br />Time for me to be a douche about the "girl with cancer book." I'm not actually, but some will think so from my opinion.<br /><br />The thing is, this book isn't quite what I expected, and something wasn't sitting right with me about the book as a symbol. Halfway through I formed my opinion as to why. I'll explain.<br /><br />This states most of my case:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851057221?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />The gripes of the above reviewer mirror most of my concerns but there's more to it than that. I have another beef with the publisher, DUTTON, an imprint of PENGUIN BOOKS. It's the same publisher as THE FAULT IN OUR STARS. That made me raise an eyebrow. And the intro of this book was the best writing in the book. And who wrote that? John Green.<br /><br />Here's my beef:<br /><br />Tragically, REALLY REALLY tragically, teenagers die from cancers. It's F'd up, but it happens. I respect Esther, her story, and I know it's important. But all of those other teens did not get books about their lives and stories, and some of them may have had just as nice families or friends or wisdoms to share. Maybe they wanted to be writers, too.<br /><br />Don't throw stones at me yet. I'm saying this: If I'm being really honest about the whole publication of this book, I think it's a bit of a cash grab. I'm sure the people who would love this book the most ar ethe people who knew Esther personally, and some of the money is probably going to a foundation. Still..... I opened this review by saying I didn't want to be a douche, and I don't think I'm being one, but this feels cash-grabby.<br /><br />Look, when the biggest YA book of the decade is still rolling out millions of copies, and months before the big movie premiere, this rolls out? My other eyebrow goes up.<br /><br />Believe it or not, and I know I'm getting controversial and probably pissing people off, I picked up this book knowing that I would give it five stars, FIVE!, and recommend it to anyone with a heartbeat. I WAS READY TO FALL IN LOVE, BE INSPIRED! -- but I cannot. I was not.<br /><br />It's all laid out in John Green's introduction: Esther, a wonderful girl, bumped into a famous author at a convention, and then she got famous because of him and he got more famous because of her, and John Green's publisher approached Esther Earl's parents, (but no other teens with cancer because they didn't know John Green) and published this book. A weighty volume, beautifully rendering her lifetime, on dense paper with heavy subject matter.<br /><br />But as I read the first 200 pages and skimmed thoughtfully and patiently through the next 200, I asked myself -- "Besides showing how normal and sweet and generous and loving she is, and inspiring us to live better like most cancer stories do, what specifically did Esther's life or talents impart on us that I didn't already know about being a good person already? What does she get a book nationally published while others did not?"<br /><br />I leave you to read this for yourself and answer that question.<br /><br />Did Not Finish (MARCH 2014)<br /><br />2/5<br />MH</span>
  <a data-text-id="5200023666742226929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sadie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sadie" href="/user/show/6186345-sadie">Sadie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11795831235593920668">I...wow. Okay, this is going to be difficult.<br/><br/>I mean I'm sure no one is going to see this anyway, because who honestly reads Review #3469, but I'm going to do this anyway.<br/><br/>The thing is, for a very brief time, I <i>was</i> the cancer girl. I was the one with a scarf instead of hair, I was the one with a skinny, chemo-ravaged body, I was the one who was bedridden. And as I start to tell my own story on paper, I gradually start to reach out for other people. People who understand what it feels like to be dy</span>
  <span id="freeText11795831235593920668" style="display:none">I...wow. Okay, this is going to be difficult.<br /><br />I mean I'm sure no one is going to see this anyway, because who honestly reads Review #3469, but I'm going to do this anyway.<br /><br />The thing is, for a very brief time, I <i>was</i> the cancer girl. I was the one with a scarf instead of hair, I was the one with a skinny, chemo-ravaged body, I was the one who was bedridden. And as I start to tell my own story on paper, I gradually start to reach out for other people. People who understand what it feels like to be dying quicker than other people. So I guess you could say that Esther called out to me for...well, a while.<br /><br />And you know, here's the god-honest truth: some people shine a light so brightly into this world and all of that brightness seeps into every dark corner and crevice until it no longer exists. Some of us are fortunate to know those kinds of people. Those who knew Esther were of that variety.<br /><br />This book...this, god, this beautiful, moving thing! It's a very long eulogy, admittedly, that's kind of what it feels like. But to read Esther's words, and her parents' words, and those whose lives she irrevocably changed, is to slowly know her yourself.<br /><br />And it makes her loss so particularly crushing in ways it isn't to the average joe. <br /><br />John Green's said on a number of occasions that his biggest <i>TFiOS</i> disappointment is that the one person he wants most to read it is the one person who will never have the chance. In similar fashion, the one person I now want most to meet, I never will. But I feel that I have come just slightly closer, and for that, I am forever grateful.<br /><br />Esther. Star Girl. You are the brightest star in the heavens. May you never cease to shine.</span>

<div id="review_815969267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/815969267" />
    <a title="April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13261686-april"><img alt="April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545858896p2/13261686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/815969267?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April" href="/user/show/13261686-april">April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer815969267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10493116142997989054">I know it’s cliché to say this, but I truly have never been more thrilled to receive a book in the mail. Esther is up there with J. K. Rowling and Evanna Lynch on my list of supreme role models. I’ve never spoken to Esther, but the way her friends, family, and even those like me speak about her is inspiring. She passed away from thyroid cancer when she was my age, sixteen. In those sixteen years, she left a legacy of a loving, caring, and empathetic person. In the words of her friend Teryn, “Est</span>
  <span id="freeText10493116142997989054" style="display:none">I know it’s cliché to say this, but I truly have never been more thrilled to receive a book in the mail. Esther is up there with J. K. Rowling and Evanna Lynch on my list of supreme role models. I’ve never spoken to Esther, but the way her friends, family, and even those like me speak about her is inspiring. She passed away from thyroid cancer when she was my age, sixteen. In those sixteen years, she left a legacy of a loving, caring, and empathetic person. In the words of her friend Teryn, “Esther was not perfect, but she was the epitome of how to be imperfect.”<br /><br />The book itself is beautifully organized — and even color-coded! — to tell her story, mainly with her journal entries and CaringBridge posts. Arielle, Esther and Teryn’s fellow Catitude member, designed a font of Esther’s handwriting that is used throughout the book. My usual problem with nonfiction — biographies in particular — is how impersonal they can feel. But the Earls, as they say of Esther, are welcomers. This book isn’t just sentence after sentence of facts about Esther’s life. It’s all the emotions and experiences of her, her family, and her friends from the comforting whirring of her oxygen machine to the late night Catitude chats. Catitude? I’ve never seen a group of friends quite like them, and Mr. and Mrs. Earl are among the best people I’ve had the pleasure to meet.<br /><br />Holding this book for the first time was a fantastic feeling, and reading it was even better. When you get to page 293, just remember to tell me how hard you laughed. I’d like to say a special thanks to Esther’s parents for allowing me to help with the book and for thinking of me when early copies were being sent.<br /><br />This Star Won’t Go Out. We won’t let it.<br /><br />To purchase Esther’s book, you can find sellers listed here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://tswgobook.tumblr.com/book">tswgobook.tumblr.com/book</a><br /><br />To learn more about the This Star Won’t Go Out Foundation, visit tswgo.org.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_928313489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/928313489" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17561595-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475688396p2/17561595.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928313489?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/17561595-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17561595-jessica?shelf=book-club-reads">book-club-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928313489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17830060205142644656">I have been a Nerdfighter since almost the beginning (mid-2007), and so it makes sense that I would read this book that John Green has mentioned multiple times and for which he wrote the introduction. But I would not have finished it if it weren't a book club read, and even then I almost abandoned it.<br/><br/>This is not so much a "book" as it is a giant collection of everything related to Esther Earl -- her diary entries, her family's CaringBridge updates, transcripts of some of her videos, reflections </span>
  <span id="freeText17830060205142644656" style="display:none">I have been a Nerdfighter since almost the beginning (mid-2007), and so it makes sense that I would read this book that John Green has mentioned multiple times and for which he wrote the introduction. But I would not have finished it if it weren't a book club read, and even then I almost abandoned it.<br /><br />This is not so much a "book" as it is a giant collection of everything related to Esther Earl -- her diary entries, her family's CaringBridge updates, transcripts of some of her videos, reflections by friends and family members, her dad's eulogy of her, and even pieces of some fiction she'd started writing. I understand that when someone dies, especially someone as young as Esther, those who knew them take comfort in every word they wrote and every memory others share of them. And in that way, this book is great for those who knew Esther personally. But for anyone else, it's not so much a book as the source material for what could be a book. Based on other people's reflections of Esther, it seems like there is a lot of awesomeness and inspiration that the people who knew her took from knowing her, and that could have been put together into a cohesive story, interspersed with Esther's own words.<br /><br />But reading the unedited diary entries of a teenager, even a teenager with cancer, makes me want to go burn all my old diaries. Like my own teenage writings, Esther's diaries contain stream-of-consciousness, overly dramatic retellings of every minute thing she did or thought each day, complete with frequent asides and text abbreviations that make them grating to read. I'm sure for someone who ever had a conversation with Esther or watched her videos, you could hear her personality come out in her writing, but for me it was a struggle to read. It was also a struggle to read detailed medical updates from the CaringBridge site about Esther's levels of something-or-other going up and down when I knew the eventual outcome of all those ups and downs, so I couldn't read into them the same hope or disappointment that people getting updates in the moment would have felt.<br /><br />I probably would have given this 2 stars, but the kicker was that it was so badly edited and constructed. Because it was just a giant document dump, stuff was not labeled well and it was not always clear when I was reading someone's writing and when it was a transcript (especially because Esther's writing contained plenty of "umm"s and sentence fragments). Near the end there's some writing by her dad dated 2011, followed by writing by other family members that I eventually realized was written in 2013 but wasn't dated.<br /><br />I wish someone had not been content to let this ride on the coattails of John Green / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> but had instead used it as source material to write a compelling true story about a girl with cancer who brought joy to the people around her, one that people who didn't know Esther would actually read and appreciate. As it is, this is a nice compilation for people who want to remember a girl they knew, but not worth slogging through for anyone else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17830060205142644656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2589382758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2589382758" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2589382758?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=medical">medical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2589382758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15283687403161561524">This book has been on my to-read list for a very long time. Esther Grace Earl, the dedicated namesake of John Green's <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>, tragically passed away when I was in junior high school. <i>This Star Won't Go Out</i> is quite a sad book, all things considered, but an important one - I think it's really easy to see grieving families and stories of sick kids in hospitals and to think of them as statistics, or just figures to be blindly pitied, but everyone whose life is affected by an illness</span>
  <span id="freeText15283687403161561524" style="display:none">This book has been on my to-read list for a very long time. Esther Grace Earl, the dedicated namesake of John Green's <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>, tragically passed away when I was in junior high school. <i>This Star Won't Go Out</i> is quite a sad book, all things considered, but an important one - I think it's really easy to see grieving families and stories of sick kids in hospitals and to think of them as statistics, or just figures to be blindly pitied, but everyone whose life is affected by an illness, death or condition has a story to tell, and Esther's is shared here in a way that lets readers know who she was as a person, and perhaps who she could have been if she'd been given more time.<br /><br />I'm not personally sure what to make of John Green using Esther's story in connection with <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i> (to be totally honest, I found Esther's story more interesting, although both books are good in their own ways), but I really liked this book. It's inspirational but not too preachy or full of false sentiments, and it's an honest, bittersweet and almost nostalgic portrait of a young teenager's life, both the good and the bad. It's a wonderful legacy and one that definitely should be shared. The style is a bit unorthodox for a book, and that made it even more interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15283687403161561524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_995714524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/995714524?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.S. Daley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.S. Daley" href="/user/show/1941083-c-s-daley">C.S. Daley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1941083-c-s-daley?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995714524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8785550282622700821">My sister died when I was a sophomore in high school. She was only a few years older than me and her battle with cancer took up much of her young life. Her loss left a hole in the hearts of my brothers and sisters that we still feel to this day. She was the bravest person I know and I truly believe that every ounce of bravery and compassion I have in my body I learned from her. I miss her terribly. <br/><br/>I was afraid to read this book. I read the introduction by John Green and started crying. 30 years</span>
  <span id="freeText8785550282622700821" style="display:none">My sister died when I was a sophomore in high school. She was only a few years older than me and her battle with cancer took up much of her young life. Her loss left a hole in the hearts of my brothers and sisters that we still feel to this day. She was the bravest person I know and I truly believe that every ounce of bravery and compassion I have in my body I learned from her. I miss her terribly. <br /><br />I was afraid to read this book. I read the introduction by John Green and started crying. 30 years after my sisters death it was still hard to think about it. I put the book down. Tonight I decided to read it and I am glad I did. Esther's words were powerful. Her bravery was astounding. Her words and story made me love and cherish my sister even more. I am not going to pretend like this book will cause some sort of epiphany. I also don't believe the loss of Esther or my sister or any of the people we have all lost in our lives will suddenly have meaning. Will suddenly be transformed into a happy ending. Nothing will replace the lost years. What the book did do was give me a chance to remember my sister's courage. My sister's love. This was a book worth reading. I thank Esther and her family for letting me share it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8785550282622700821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_975102969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975102969" />
    <a title="Laurence R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32492014-laurence-r"><img alt="Laurence R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577676096p2/32492014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975102969?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurence R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurence R." href="/user/show/32492014-laurence-r">Laurence R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32492014-laurence-r?shelf=dying-to-read">dying-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32492014-laurence-r?shelf=dear-friends">dear-friends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975102969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1095336210997359072">Dear Esther,<br/><br/>I do not know you, and you certainly don't know me. I mean, I was born four years later than you were and during all our lives, we've been separated by miles and miles, even by borders. I wasn't part of Nerdfighteria when you were and I don't even know if I had a Facebook account when you were still alive, let alone a Youtube account. However, your story touched me so, so, so much. <br/><br/>Life is unfair, we all know it. Some of us, like me, have been blessed enough to have a relatively easy</span>
  <span id="freeText1095336210997359072" style="display:none">Dear Esther,<br /><br />I do not know you, and you certainly don't know me. I mean, I was born four years later than you were and during all our lives, we've been separated by miles and miles, even by borders. I wasn't part of Nerdfighteria when you were and I don't even know if I had a Facebook account when you were still alive, let alone a Youtube account. However, your story touched me so, so, so much. <br /><br />Life is unfair, we all know it. Some of us, like me, have been blessed enough to have a relatively easy life so far and to only see illnesses and death from a very far away perspective. However, reading your journals, watching your videos, and hearing people talk about you has made me realize how unfair your life was. How could a person so radiant, so cheerful and so smart like you have to go such hard times? I know from your own words that you became okay with the fact that you had cancer and that your faith has helped you a lot with that. This is a truly fantastic thing, especially from the point of view of an atheist like me. I have always envied people who belong to a religion, because I can imagine how much easier it can be to think that everything happens for a reason. This book proved my thoughts, because you made it sound so easy.<br /><br />I loved the person you were, or at least the idea I got of the person you were. I know that I could never get to know you as much as I want to, because I've only seen a glimpse of the person you were, but I do know that everyone around you was lucky to have you. I don't know what you would think of people like me, who read your book, your journal, even, watch your videos, hear your friends talking about you and end up loving you. I hope you'd like it, because everyone has described you as a 'welcomer', a loving person who accepted everyone. I love that about you. That's the way more people should be. In a way, you're a bit like how everyone should be: caring, passionate, intelligent, confident. I'm not saying you were perfect, but I do think you were an awesome person. <br /><br />My thoughts go to your friends, to your family, to your cats. As weird as it must be for them to see you become some sort of celebrity, I hope they accept the support we are willing to give them, because your book has truly made my eyes open. From Heaven (because I know that's where you are, even though I am in no way religious), I hope that you're happy that your cause has brought so many of us together to make the world a better place to live in, even though you will never have this chance again and it's breaking my heart. Don't forget to be awesome, Esther, while we'll never forget how bright a star you were.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1095336210997359072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/923696923" />
    <a title="kari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207055-kari"><img alt="kari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/923696923?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kari" href="/user/show/2207055-kari">kari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=2014">2014</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer923696923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13115219230883518707">Prepare to shed some tears with this one. <br/>The story of Esther Grace Earl's too-short life is beautifully contained with these pages. There are journal entries, transcripts of some internet conversations, commentary from her parents and friends, drawings. <br/>What struck me as a reader is that Esther sounds like just an ordinary girl, musing about the things teenage girls think about coupled with some very deep thoughts about life or the loss of her life and what she has and possibly will miss out on</span>
  <span id="freeText13115219230883518707" style="display:none">Prepare to shed some tears with this one. <br />The story of Esther Grace Earl's too-short life is beautifully contained with these pages. There are journal entries, transcripts of some internet conversations, commentary from her parents and friends, drawings. <br />What struck me as a reader is that Esther sounds like just an ordinary girl, musing about the things teenage girls think about coupled with some very deep thoughts about life or the loss of her life and what she has and possibly will miss out on. I think that she would like being thought of as ordinary. And yet there is something extraordinary about her as well. She was courageous because she had to be, but that wasn't a simple thing, nor was that all that she was. Funny, smart, sometimes sad or angry, loving and loved.<br />This book needs to be experienced. Although well over 400 pages it is a fast read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13115219230883518707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_840261533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840261533" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7155515-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323570692p2/7155515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840261533?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/7155515-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840261533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1115118915475709099">I rarely take the time to review books, mostly because I don't tend to have super interesting things to say, but this is different. I had the pleasure of meeting Esther via Skype at Infinitus 2010 and it is something that I will never forget. Cancer is a tough subject for me, as my dad passed away from cancer in April 2010. Meeting Esther just a couple of months later was both hard and touching but I was immensely impressed with how well she dealt with her illness. A year after Esther passed awa</span>
  <span id="freeText1115118915475709099" style="display:none">I rarely take the time to review books, mostly because I don't tend to have super interesting things to say, but this is different. I had the pleasure of meeting Esther via Skype at Infinitus 2010 and it is something that I will never forget. Cancer is a tough subject for me, as my dad passed away from cancer in April 2010. Meeting Esther just a couple of months later was both hard and touching but I was immensely impressed with how well she dealt with her illness. A year after Esther passed away, I became ill and I lived with an undiagnosed illness for the next year and a half. While I was lucky enough to find a cure for my illness, living with a disease sucks. And unless you have been in that situation, you cannot come close to understanding the exhaustion, the hopelessness, and how useless you feel. Reading Esther's entries helped me to come to term with the feelings I had during my illness because she UNDERSTOOD EXACTLY. Of course she did. And while I wouldn't wish that kind of experience on anyone, I will always cherish this book for helping me see the hope and light in life, no matter what.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1115118915475709099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_817545060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/817545060" />
    <a title="Gypsy White" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15925880-gypsy-white"><img alt="Gypsy White" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495148706p2/15925880.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/817545060?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gypsy White" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gypsy White" href="/user/show/15925880-gypsy-white">Gypsy White</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15925880-gypsy-white?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15925880-gypsy-white?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15925880-gypsy-white?shelf=literal-tears-fell">literal-tears-fell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15925880-gypsy-white?shelf=2014-adventures">2014-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15925880-gypsy-white?shelf=sad-but-good">sad-but-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer817545060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6614040941232891926">Just a note: I won this in a Goodreads Giveaway. Thanks Penguin!<br/><i> "But even in her final days, Esther was wholly alive, as alive as anyone else, and so even though everyone who loved her understood she was dying, her death was still a terrible shock to me. She did not leave slowly, but all at once, because even when she could not get out of bed, she found ways to be fully alive: to play with her friends, to crack jokes, to love and to be loved. And then she was gone, all at once."</i> <u>-John Green's i</u></span>
  <span id="freeText6614040941232891926" style="display:none">Just a note: I won this in a Goodreads Giveaway. Thanks Penguin!<br><i> "But even in her final days, Esther was wholly alive, as alive as anyone else, and so even though everyone who loved her understood she was dying, her death was still a terrible shock to me. She did not leave slowly, but all at once, because even when she could not get out of bed, she found ways to be fully alive: to play with her friends, to crack jokes, to love and to be loved. And then she was gone, all at once."</i> <u>-John Green's intro</u><br>Yeah, that's how it starts off. If you can make it through this whole book without shedding a single tear, you have balls of steel. <br>I would love to summarize this in my own words, but I'm going to let Esther do it for me: "This is a story about a girl that went through a life changing experience known as Thyroid Cancer. It's not one of those dramatic "based on a true story" cancer things, especially since Thyroid Cancer is not as bad as caner. It's a story about me, Esther Earl, having a sickness that's pretty scary."<br>This book could actually be labeled more as a diary. It had multiple articles in it from Esther's own diary to Skype chats with her online friends. Going into this book I knew nothing about Esther Grace Earl, in fact (I feel terrible saying this) I didn't even know she existed. I thought The Fault in Our Stars was something Green had just made up. After reading his inspiration for it, I now view TFIOS differently. Esther was an amazing girl who was so much more mature and spiritual than most teenagers. One quote of her's really made me sit down and think: "If one person sits down at their computer one day and types one word, does that affect the future?" Like dang, she was only fourteen when she wrote that down. She was just too kind and wise for this world, and God had to take her back. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383612451ra/6611098.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>At the beginning of the book, you know the date of her death. Most diary entires have dates on the top. The further you go and the closer the horrible date comes, the more pain you feel for the family knowing certain things she does will be her last. If only this were fiction, it wouldn't be so bad. But it's not. This happens to real people all the time. And this happened to the Earl family. The articles from family and friends are so heart-wrenching, you can feel their pain and it will make your heart feel funny.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391913321ra/8474829.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There's only two negative things about this book, and neither of them have to do with Esther (because how can you feel any negativity towards such an amazing and bright girl?!). 1) I have a hardcover copy and it's super heavy and hard to hold. It's not a big deal, just made it a little uncomfortable to read. <br>2)Some of the dates were out of order, so just make sure you're keeping track of them. I don't know if it was intentional or just an editing glitch. <br>OH! And one more thing before I go. Do not under any circumstance read pages 320-330, unless you like getting your heart ripped out of its rib caged and smashed to pieces by a demon wearing soccer cleats. <br><i> As far as I have seen, to know you is literally to love you. </i> John Green to Esther <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392665744ra/8591709.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6614040941232891926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1492810497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1492810497" />
    <a title="Stella Wenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24629412-stella-wenny"><img alt="Stella Wenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565190915p2/24629412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1492810497?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stella Wenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stella Wenny" href="/user/show/24629412-stella-wenny">Stella Wenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786020989150" href="/book/show/25477364-this-star-won-t-go-out">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1492810497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14217520700877035242"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>Does having terminal illness somehow makes people stronger? I wonder a lot about this throughout the book. Having both my parents suffered cancer (specifically my mother who had the same trouble breathing without oxygen nasal cannula like Esther) and having so many friends in net world, I can relate to this book so much. Perhaps that's one of the reasons why I wanted to read this book, to remember my parents, to remember their suffering, so that I still remember to honor and respect th</span>
  <span id="freeText14217520700877035242" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />Does having terminal illness somehow makes people stronger? I wonder a lot about this throughout the book. Having both my parents suffered cancer (specifically my mother who had the same trouble breathing without oxygen nasal cannula like Esther) and having so many friends in net world, I can relate to this book so much. Perhaps that's one of the reasons why I wanted to read this book, to remember my parents, to remember their suffering, so that I still remember to honor and respect them, to keep them alive inside of me.<br /><br />So, does having terminal illness somehow make people stronger? Do people become stronger when they know that they don't have much time leave? Or do people become stronger because families and friends would come to you and giving you much supports and loves? I wouldn't know the answer to these questions, but I always admire how my mother became so much stronger back then, and in this book I see Esther becomes stronger because of her illness.<br /><br />It's amazing to see how big her influence to this world. So many charities held to honor her short life. So many people felt touched and moved and did good things because of the ripple effect of her death. This star would certainly never go out.<br /><br />Also, I really understand how Esther's friends felt when Esther died. Their net world was in deep mourning but their real world went on like nothing happened. I have many online friends that I'd be depressed for if they were dying. Online friends are still real friends.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>The measure of a friendship is not its physicality but its significance. Good friendships, online or off, urge us toward empathy; they give us comfort and also pull us out of the prisons of our selves.</b>
</i><br /><br />Actually, this book is more 4 stars to me, there are quite many topics in Esther's writings that I don't really care about. But I cried hard when I reach the part that Esther died. I cried in my office. So half a star added. And I can't still get over of how awesome and beautiful and fitting the title is. This Star Won't Go Out—that's like the most beautiful title I've ever come across.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>When loved ones die, people always say, “Don’t be sad. I’m sure they would have wanted you to be happy.” I’m sure that’s true. But let’s be realistic here, people also want to be missed. It is every person’s nightmare to leave the world behind as if they had never been there at all.</b>
</i><br /><br />Thanks to Belle/Yuki for letting me borrow this book :*</span>
  <a data-text-id="14217520700877035242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_937726039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937726039" />
    <a title="Allegra S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30601872-allegra-s"><img alt="Allegra S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400012509p2/30601872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/937726039?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allegra S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allegra S" href="/user/show/30601872-allegra-s">Allegra S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30601872-allegra-s?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30601872-allegra-s?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30601872-allegra-s?shelf=emotionally-moving">emotionally-moving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30601872-allegra-s?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937726039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2018743803212679750">It feels weird to review this book. What Esther wrote she wrote for own eyes, it wasn't something she originally meant to have published. It wouldn't be right to critique her thoughts. In fact, I really enjoyed reading her thoughts. I will be mainly critiquing the organization and presentation of these thoughts as a book.<br/><br/>People who will enjoy this book are: people who knew Esther either personally or through her online presence, people who want to see the connection between her and John Green's </span>
  <span id="freeText2018743803212679750" style="display:none">It feels weird to review this book. What Esther wrote she wrote for own eyes, it wasn't something she originally meant to have published. It wouldn't be right to critique her thoughts. In fact, I really enjoyed reading her thoughts. I will be mainly critiquing the organization and presentation of these thoughts as a book.<br /><br />People who will enjoy this book are: people who knew Esther either personally or through her online presence, people who want to see the connection between her and John Green's novel TFIOS, teens struggling with serious illness that need someone to relate to, particularly if they are Christian.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the excerpts written by John Green. I also thought the presentation of the book was amazing. The photos they chose were perfect, and I love the full-colour print on every page. Where I struggled with this book and failed to give it 5-stars was because it didn't quite live up to certain expectations. It's not quite a memoir or a published diary. Firstly, it starts at a point in Esther's life where she has had cancer already for two years and it is 200 pages of her diary and letters talking about her family, struggling with her illness, and finding a renewed faith. Then there are quite a few pages of her parent's online blog to inform friends and family of Esther's condition for a year. Then it jumps back in time and suddenly the whole book is about Esther's involvement with a group of online friends interspersed with her parent's blog. If I hadn't read John Green's introduction I think I would have been pretty confused about what was happening in her life.<br /><br />First of all - they should have arranged everything in absolute chronological order, otherwise it's really too confusing to follow. Her parents said that Esther wrote every single night, so they obviously had a lot of material to work with. When I think of something like this I think of the Diary of Anne Frank and how her father only slightly edited out the parts that were too sexually explicit. I think they should have actually put MORE of Esther's diary entries into the book, even small excerpts of fiction along the way. It skips over months of time, so it's clear that things have been edited. Secondly, I know it's hard to boil a person's life down to one story, but when you create a book you have to take an 'angle' on the story in order to make it readable. It could have been either her diary from when she was diagnosed until her death, OR they could have had several entries when she described her loneliness and then how she found happiness in having an online presence. Third, though I love the messages that all of her internet friends - I wish they hadn't put them all at the end! It reads like a really long eulogy. I wish they had had various entries and excerpts from her friends interspersed with her writing so you got a better sense of how they became friends and supported Esther in her loneliness. This would have been particularly interesting if they had some of the messages between John Green and Esther. I think if they had changed the organization a bit I would have gotten a better sense of who Esther was as a person. As it stands things are bit choppy in my mind.<br /><br />I did enjoy several things that were written. One thing that stood out to me was that her father was quite religious and along the way you start to see subtle clues that he was beginning to question his faith. In one of the blog entries he writes "our faith remains, but it is changed". In the end though my favourite part was Esther's message which said: "Just be happy. And if you can't be happy, do things that make you happy. And if you can't do that, do nothing with the people that make you happy." Isn't that the meaning of it all? :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2018743803212679750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="TABI⁷ (ᕗツ)ᕗ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TABI⁷ (ᕗツ)ᕗ" href="/user/show/4325322-tabi">TABI⁷ (ᕗツ)ᕗ</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1018802199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16447032003080705598">This is the story of an amazing girl who faced death with a smile on her face and a twinkle in her eye. It's a story about a girl who lived, was real; loved and was loved back. <br/><br/>This isn't a story to hate, only to read. As you read, you will see just how bright of a light Esther was, and no amount of celebrity friends or popularity made her that or changed her. She was a girl, she lived, and then sadly she died. It's not a glamorous story, nor is it a unique one. <br/><br/>The only unique thing about this,</span>
  <span id="freeText16447032003080705598" style="display:none">This is the story of an amazing girl who faced death with a smile on her face and a twinkle in her eye. It's a story about a girl who lived, was real; loved and was loved back. <br /><br />This isn't a story to hate, only to read. As you read, you will see just how bright of a light Esther was, and no amount of celebrity friends or popularity made her that or changed her. She was a girl, she lived, and then sadly she died. It's not a glamorous story, nor is it a unique one. <br /><br />The only unique thing about this, was Esther herself. When you read this book, you will laugh, cry, and feel things the way she did. You will wish she was alive so you could hug her and tell her just how awesome she is and how strong to be smiling through all of this. <br /><br />Yes, she is one in a million stories and yes there are other children who deserve just as much attention as she did. So don't complain about the ones who didn't get a book like Esther did. Read this book, then go find those other childrens stories. As long as they are remembered and read, even if they are not, they are just as important as Esther was.<br /><br />Don't forget to be awesome.</span>

<div id="review_2866499350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2866499350" />
    <a title="Erica Henry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90888099-erica-henry"><img alt="Erica Henry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598222633p2/90888099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2866499350?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Henry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Henry" href="/user/show/90888099-erica-henry">Erica Henry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90888099-erica-henry?shelf=books-read-in-2019">books-read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90888099-erica-henry?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2866499350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14562781143959390552">What can I possibly say about this story? This book is about a girl, a very young girl, diagnosed with thyroid cancer. She goes through so much all the while staying so positive. In her 16 years on this Earth, Esther made quite an impact on a lot of people and made so many friends, including the famous author John Green. Although she was very sick, she loved reaching out and tried to help those who were sick too. This little girl was full of so much love and hope. She was a lover of many things </span>
  <span id="freeText14562781143959390552" style="display:none">What can I possibly say about this story? This book is about a girl, a very young girl, diagnosed with thyroid cancer. She goes through so much all the while staying so positive. In her 16 years on this Earth, Esther made quite an impact on a lot of people and made so many friends, including the famous author John Green. Although she was very sick, she loved reaching out and tried to help those who were sick too. This little girl was full of so much love and hope. She was a lover of many things and she was a fighter. She fought and fought up until the very end.<br />We all should strive to be like that little girl. We need to learn to show others love, even if some of them don't even deserve it. Love is so much stronger then death and that is something that is taught in this book. Esther's words, "Just be happy. And if you can't be happy, do things that make you happy. Or do nothing with people that make you happy." Those words alone definitely have impacted me in a good way. I want to strive to be just the way Esther was when she was alive. Live, love, and be loved. We are put on this Earth to live our best life and we need to live it without fear.</span>
