<div id="review_2572710644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2572710644" />
    <a title="Lynette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20544478-lynette"><img alt="Lynette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527696714p2/20544478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2572710644?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynette" href="/user/show/20544478-lynette">Lynette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20544478-lynette?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572710644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3459043686353792479">I haven’t cried like this for a book in a long time, possibly ever. This hit me personally so hard and feels so relevant to my current life I had to pick it up. I’ll elaborate more later in the review, but now for the book itself.<br/><br/>It’s so hard to capture the essence of someone’s life, but through family, friends and even Esther’s own telling of her life, you fully get an understanding of the wonderful person she was. How many lives she touched in her short time here. She did fully live her life, </span>
  <span id="freeText3459043686353792479" style="display:none">I haven’t cried like this for a book in a long time, possibly ever. This hit me personally so hard and feels so relevant to my current life I had to pick it up. I’ll elaborate more later in the review, but now for the book itself.<br /><br />It’s so hard to capture the essence of someone’s life, but through family, friends and even Esther’s own telling of her life, you fully get an understanding of the wonderful person she was. How many lives she touched in her short time here. She did fully live her life, and that is heart warming. Her impact on the world is still happening and she is influencing people she has never met before. That shows the power of a meaningful, caring and “graceful” life. One tiny negative, was this book at times felt like it was meant to just make money. I know that wasn’t the intent, and it must have been extremely difficult to write this, going through diaries, memories and recalling her hardest times. The intro just seemed disjointed, but I can’t even comprehend how to start a book about a loved one’s life. Again, no fault to the family or doctors or anyone, I cannot even begin to understand how difficult it was.<br /><br />Now, I was debating if I should add my other thoughts...but I believe I will. This has no reflection of the book itself, but is more on how it affected me personally. Every reader enjoys this lovely pastime for different reasons, and that can vary even from book to book. I find that you can find similarities or even little revelations in the most random books. Even the most beloved high fantasy novel can have you identify with a certain situation or give you a statement that makes you have to pause and really think it over.<br /><br />Now that the foundation is set, onto my thoughts. I highly identified with Esther, not that I have cancer, but I have some health issues happening. This may sound awful, but I wish I could be as confident as she was and say “yup I have cancer and it sucks”. I can’t say that. I’ve been to 14? 15? doctors now, and no one can figure out what it is. It was thrown out there yesterday that there could be several issues happening. Esther had many great things to say in her diaries: I don’t know what tomorrow brings, all I can do is hope and pray for the best. Her acceptance and loving, uplifting nature is something I hope I’ve always done, but will for sure be focusing on. I also understand her little outburst of frustration and not wanting to burden anyone when she has them. This book was also eye opening in the parental side. I know this is hard on my parents, especially being in a completely different state as them. Whenever Esther’s dad wrote about how he felt throughout Esther’s battle, I felt my heart breaking, knowing that’s exactly what my dad feels. There was a line that completely drove the breath out of me. “I should be walking my daughter down the aisle, not planning her funeral”. <br /><br />Well, now that I’ve also began crying writing this review, I think that means it’s time to wrap it up! Quote time: “Love is stronger than Death” and DFTBA (Don’t forget to be awesome) ❤️</span>
  <a data-text-id="3459043686353792479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_830342651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/830342651" />
    <a title="Charlotte Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones"><img alt="Charlotte Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361900141p2/8943949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/830342651?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte Jones" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones">Charlotte Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer830342651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5224441236576546252">This book is the story and experiences of Esther Earl, a girl that John knew and was a huge part of the online Nerdfighter community, who unfortunately died of cancer at just 16 in 2010. I can’t claim to have known her but her story is one that I think everyone in the community knows a little about and I just wanted to read her story in her own words, as well as from the viewpoint of the people around her.<br/><br/>I couldn’t review this book in the way I usually would because you cannot put a non-fiction</span>
  <span id="freeText5224441236576546252" style="display:none">This book is the story and experiences of Esther Earl, a girl that John knew and was a huge part of the online Nerdfighter community, who unfortunately died of cancer at just 16 in 2010. I can’t claim to have known her but her story is one that I think everyone in the community knows a little about and I just wanted to read her story in her own words, as well as from the viewpoint of the people around her.<br /><br />I couldn’t review this book in the way I usually would because you cannot put a non-fiction real-life story into the same group as fiction, so this will be more of a discussion and a recommendation than a review.<br /><br />From the beginning of this, I was in tears. John Green’s introduction was the most heart-warming yet devastating things that I have read. I always knew that there was a connection between Esther and The Fault in our Stars but reading this book really proved just how much Esther’s presence effected John and how her story is one that needs to be seen as complex and human, and how Hazel is not Esther, though without Esther, Hazel wouldn’t exist.<br /><br />The book itself really captures the feeling of the book. Although it is sad, I like that the publisher decided on a bright cover and packaging for this book because it stops it feeling like a bleak depressing story. Of course, it is sad but the colourful pages, the inclusion of photographs, drawings and handwritten passages, make it a lot more approachable and real. Esther was a real person, a complex and unique individual and I think that this book really does reflect that and stops it being another cancer story.<br /><br />One thing that was a little odd for me to read about was Esther’s faith. I am not a religious person and usually reading about someone’s religion would distance me from the book, but in this case I completely understood her faith and her belief in it. In such a dire situation it was refreshing to read Esther’s words on faith and her cancer in all its honestly. She is completely honest in these pages and it just adds to the sadness of the book. As John Green has said many times, Esther was a young person who was not defined by her illness and I think that this definitely comes through in these pages.<br /><br />I have said that this book is sad; I mean I cried through the majority of its pages, but it is also full of hope and love and happy memories. Esther is someone that will continue to inspire me in my life and I urge you to pick up this book and be inspired by Esther’s story too. This is one of the most human stories that I have read and I can’t recommend it enough.<br /> DFTBA (don’t forget to be awesome).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5224441236576546252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_825527864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825527864" />
    <a title="Jillyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5818960-jillyn"><img alt="Jillyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502241239p2/5818960.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/825527864?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillyn" href="/user/show/5818960-jillyn">Jillyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer825527864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7470505585738198647">I'm left not really knowing what to say about this book, if I'm being completely honest. I am going to keep this review as simple as I can, while still giving my opinion on the book itself not the topic of the book. <br/><br/>Like a lot of other readers, I picked this up after reading The Fault in Our Stars. I wasn't entirely sure what to expect. I'm not a part of the Nerdfighter community, so I had little to no information about Esther prior to this book's release. When I realized what the story was abou</span>
  <span id="freeText7470505585738198647" style="display:none">I'm left not really knowing what to say about this book, if I'm being completely honest. I am going to keep this review as simple as I can, while still giving my opinion on the book itself not the topic of the book. <br /><br />Like a lot of other readers, I picked this up after reading The Fault in Our Stars. I wasn't entirely sure what to expect. I'm not a part of the Nerdfighter community, so I had little to no information about Esther prior to this book's release. When I realized what the story was about, and saw that it was prefaced by John Green, I knew I wanted to read it. <br /><br />This hardcover is really, really long. However it's not that much text. There's a lot of pictures and transcripts taken in letter or email format, making it an easier read than it appears to be. I do think it was very poorly organized as a book. This book includes a lot of Esther's writings from her journals, letters, and internet happenings. But there's no real chapters or distinctions, so one minute you're on a diary page, and the next you're reading insight from one of her doctors. I also feel like this book dragged on longer than it needed to. I feel horrible saying that, but it was just kind of boring after awhile. I know how that sounds, and I'm so sorry, but it's true. Esther was also a very religious/spiritual person, and there's heavy doses of God in this book. That's nowhere near a bad thing, but it's not something I anticipated going into the book. <br /><br />Honestly, Esther seems like she was a great person. She comes off as very kind and optimistic, and everyone certainly seemed to love her right until the end. And I think that's great that, as the title suggests, their star won't go out. I hope she inspires sick kids everywhere to be positive and to keep fighting and keep smiling.<br /><br />I've read quite a few cancer memoirs, and because of that I can't say this book really taught me anything. That said, it was interesting to see cancer through a kid's perspective. Sad, of course. But interesting nonetheless.<br /><br />I think that this book (already does) will gain lots of fans who will find inspiration and solace in the words and life of Esther Earl. I think it is worth reading once. However, I don't think I will be rereading it in the future, and I don't know that I will remember this book further down the road. <br /><br />It's not you, book. It's me.<br /><br />This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://bitchesnprose.blogspot.com/2015/08/review-this-star-wont-go-out-by-esther.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Bitches n Prose</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7470505585738198647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gc6XoGTgCcDlH1FfAzN0USnBswPIoJ/eImDs3q3cKtazMn1Z4LFZ7TeWBPS9UG/73sc5li3ZxxSgGCOqn1MzXg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Km1razi4Y77rbHRcqFxlpvJi0K/XeHP6Gja7gEuAVt8YkYGSvOkzkznlIfcWP34MBWRaOjIBKzCYTnT0eQ9PVw==')})
  }
//]]>
